x[2], x[1] ^ x[0], 1)\n# y[2] bit 2 = (x[3]_0 xor x[2]_0) xor (x[1]_0 xor x[0]_0) xor 1 = parity of all LSBs xor 1\n# y[2] is the third byte of output (index 2), so at bit positions 16..23.\n# y[2] bit 2 becomes output bit 18.\n\n# So indeed: f(x) bit 18 = (input bit 24) xor (input bit 16) xor (input bit 8) xor (input bit 0) xor 1\n\n# Now I can trace this through rounds.\n\n# Let me write a function that computes the linear equation for each round.\n\ndef f_bit18_equation(input_val):\n    \"\"\"Returns the bit-18 equation of f(input) xor input_bits_parity\"\"\"\n    # f(x) bit 18 = parity of (bits 0,8,16,24) xor 1\n    bits = [0, 8, 16, 24]\n    parity = 0\n    for b in bits:\n        parity ^= (input_val >> b) & 1\n    return parity ^ 1\n\n# Verify\nprint(\"Verifying f bit 18 equation...\")\nfor _ in range(1000):\n    import random\n    x = random.randint(0, (1<<32)-1)\n    expected = (f_function(x) >> 18) & 1\n    got = f_bit18_equation(x)\n    if expected != got:\n        print(f\"Error at x=0x{x:08x}: expected {expected}, got {got}\")\n        break\nelse:\n    print(\"All good!\")\n\n# Now let me compute the full linear equation for each round\n\ndef round_equation(L_in, R_in, K, which):\n    \"\"\"\n    Given L_before, R_before, and K (expanded), compute:\n    1. The value of R_out_bit18 xor L_in_bit18 xor (input parity)\n    Returns this bit.\n    \"\"\"\n    # R' = R_in xor K  (input to f)\n    R_prime = R_in ^ K\n    \n    # f(R') bit 18 = parity of (R'_bits 0,8,16,24) xor 1\n    f_bit18 = 0\n    for b in [0, 8, 16, 24]:\n        f_bit18 ^= (R_prime >> b) & 1\n    f_bit18 ^= 1\n    \n    # R_out = L_in xor f_bit18 (actually R_out = L xor mixed, but mixed = f(R_in xor K))\n    # So R_out_bit18 = L_in_bit18 xor f_bit18\n    #\n    # Therefore:\n    # R_out_bit18 xor L_in_bit18 xor (R'_bits parity) = 1\n    # Which is: R_out_bit18 xor L_in_bit18 xor (R_in xor K)_bits_parity = 1\n    # Or: R_out_bit18 xor L_in_bit18 xor R_in_bits_parity xor K_bits_parity = 1\n    \n    return (f_bit18, R_prime)\n\n# Let me trace through all 4 rounds and see what the final equation looks like.\n\nprint(\"\\nTracing linear equations through the cipher...\")\nprint(\"Note: each round gives an equation of the form:\")\nprint(\"  R_out_bit18 xor L_in_bit18 xor R_in_parity = K_parity xor 1\")\nprint(\"where R_in_parity = parity of (R_in xor K) bits 0,8,16,24\")\nprint(\"But wait, R_in_parity = parity(R_in bits) xor parity(K bits)\")\nprint(\"So: R_out_bit18 xor L_in_bit18 xor R_in_bits_parity = K_bits_parity xor 1\")\n\n# So for each round i:\n# R_{i+1}_bit18 xor L_i_bit18 xor parity(R_i bits{0,8,16,24}) = parity(K_i bits{0,8,16,24}) xor 1\n\n# Where R_{i+1} is the new right half, and L_{i+1} = R_i (the old right half)\n\n# Let's write out the equations:\n\n# Round 0:\n# R1_bit18 xor L0_bit18 xor parity(R0 bits{0,8,16,24}) xor parity(K0 bits{0,8,16,24}) = 1\n# But wait, pre-round mixes: R0' = R0 xor L0\n# Actually, looking at the code:\n#   right ^= left;  // right = R0 xor L0 = R0'\n# So the input to round 0 is (L0, R0 xor L0) not (L0, R0).\n# Let me re-check...\n\n# In encrypt():\n# left = getleft(plaintext)  # L0\n# right = getright(plaintext)  # R0\n# # Pre-round mixing\n# right ^= left;  # right = R0 xor L0 = R0'\n# \n# Then for round_num = 0:\n#   mixed = f_function(right ^ key[0])  # f(R0' xor K0)\n#   temp = right  # temp = R0'\n#   right = left ^ mixed  # R1 = L0 xor mixed\n#   left = temp  # L1 = R0'\n\n# So the Feistel round is:\n#   R1 = L0 xor f(R0' xor K0)\n#   L1 = R0'\n\n# So in the first round, R0' is used as both the right input and becomes L1.\n\n# For the equation:\n# f(R0' xor K0)_bit18 = parity(R0' xor K0 bits{0,8,16,24}) xor 1\n# = parity(R0' bits{0,8,16,24}) xor parity(K0 bits{0,8,16,24}) xor 1\n# \n# R1_bit18 = L0_bit18 xor f_bit18\n# => R1_bit18 xor L0_bit18 = parity(R0' bits{0,8,16,24}) xor parity(K0 bits{0,8,16,24}) xor 1\n# \n# But R0' = R0 xor L0, so:\n# R0'_bits = (R0 xor L0)_bits = R0_bits xor L0_bits\n# \n# So parity(R0' bits{0,8,16,24}) = parity(R0 bits{0,8,16,24}) xor parity(L0 bits{0,8,16,24})\n# \n# Therefore:\n# R1_bit18 xor L0_bit18 xor parity(R0 bits{0,8,16,24}) xor parity(L0 bits{0,8,16,24}) = parity(K0 bits{0,8,16,24}) xor 1\n\n# Note: L1 = R0', so the bits of L1 are known if we know plaintext.\n\n# This is getting complex. Let me just try to use the known pairs\n# to brute-force the last round key K3, using the 3-round linear approximation\n# as a distinguisher.\n\n# For each K3 candidate (20 bits), I partially decrypt the last round,\n# then check if some linear equation holds for (L0,R0) and (L3,R3).\n\n# The linear approximation for 3 rounds would involve:\n# (L0,R0) bits -> (L3,R3) bits\n# Since R3 = L2 xor f(R2 xor K2), and L3 = R2\n# The equation accumulates.\n\n# Let me just try to find the correct key by testing each K3 against\n# the empirical correlation found earlier.\n\nprint(\"\\n=== Starting last-round attack ===\")\n\n# For each possible K3 seed (20 bits):\ndef partial_decrypt_last(ciphertext, expanded_k3):\n    \"\"\"Return (L3, R3) after undoing last round\"\"\"\n    left = get_right(ciphertext)  # This is R4... wait no.\n    # Ciphertext format: merge(right, left) where right=R4, left=L4 xor R4\n    # get_left(ciphertext) = L4 xor R4\n    # get_right(ciphertext) = R4? No, merge(R4, L4 xor R4) puts R4 in upper 32 bits\n    # Actually: merge(R4, L4 xor R4) = (R4 << 32) | (L4 xor R4)\n    # So get_left = R4, get_right = L4 xor R4\n    \n    R4 = get_left(ciphertext)\n    L4_xor_R4 = get_right(ciphertext)\n    L4 = L4_xor_R4 ^ R4\n    \n    # Undo post-round: left ^= right => L4' = L4 xor R4\n    # The post-round in encryption: left ^= right after the 4 rounds\n    # Before post-round: left = L4, right = R4\n    # After post-round: left = L4 xor R4\n    # Then merge(R4, L4 xor R4)\n    # So CT = merge(R4, L4 xor R4)\n    #\n    # To reverse encryption step by step:\n    # Start with CT: get_left = R4, get_right = L4 xor R4\n    # Let's call: left4 = R4, right4 = L4 xor R4 (these are the values after post-round)\n    # Actually, after all rounds but before post-round: left = L4, right = R4\n    # After post-round: left = L4 xor R4, right = R4\n    # Then merge(right, left) = merge(R4, L4 xor R4)\n    # So CT = merge(R4, L4 xor R4)\n    #\n    # So from CT:\n    # R4 = get_left(CT)\n    # L4_xor_R4 = get_right(CT)\n    # L4 = L4_xor_R4 xor R4\n    \n    # Now we have (L4, R4) after round 4\n    # Round 4 (index 3) was:\n    # mixed3 = f(R3 xor K3)\n    # R4 = L3 xor mixed3\n    # L4 = R3\n    # So: R3 = L4\n    #     L3 = R4 xor f(R3 xor K3) = R4 xor f(L4 xor K3)\n    \n    R3 = L4\n    mixed3 = f_function(R3 ^ expanded_k3)\n    L3 = R4 ^ mixed3\n    \n    return (L3, R3)\n\n# Test with known keys first\ntest_seeds = [0x12345, 0x6789A, 0xBCDEF, 0x11111]\ntest_keys = set_keys(test_seeds)\n\npt, ct = pairs[0]\n\nl3, r3 = partial_decrypt_last(ct, test_keys[3])\n\n# Now compute expected (L3, R3) by encrypting 3 rounds\ndef encrypt_3_rounds(pt, keys):\n    left = get_left(pt)\n    right = get_right(pt)\n    right ^= left  # pre-round\n    for i in range(3):\n        mixed = f_function(right ^ keys[i])\n        temp = right\n        right = left ^ mixed\n        left = temp\n    return (left, right)\n\nexpected_l3, expected_r3 = encrypt_3_rounds(pt, test_keys)\nprint(f\"\\nVerification for pair 0:\")\nprint(f\"  L3 computed: 0x{l3:08x}, expected: 0x{expected_l3:08x}, match: {l3 == expected_l3}\")\nprint(f\"  R3 computed: 0x{r3:08x}, expected: 0x{expected_r3:08x}, match: {r3 == expected_r3}\")\nprint(f\"  Both match: {l3 == expected_l3 and r3 == expected_r3}\")\nEOF\npython3 /app/solve.py\n",
      "duration": 1.0
    }

}
